## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science / solid mechanics)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws describing elastic/plastic deformation and thermal softening/thermal strain in solids. Typical relationships include temperature-dependent elastic modulus, thermal expansion offsets, and nonlinear (hardening) stress–strain curves with temperature affecting stiffness and strength.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness changes with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (power law): sigma = c0 * T**c1 * epsilon (empirical stiffness scaling with temperature)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain subtraction: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * (T + c2)) (stress from mechanical strain plus thermal expansion offset; c2 often represents -T_ref)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (moderate-strain nonlinearity with thermal softening/stiffening)
- Power-law hardening (Hollomon-type) with T-dependent strength: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (work-hardening-like curvature; temperature shifts level)
- Exponential hardening (Voce-type in strain only): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (approach to saturation stress vs strain)
- Voce-type with thermal softening factor: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon))) * (1 + c3 * T) (strain saturation combined with temperature effect)
- Ramberg–Osgood-style implicit/explicit stress form (explicit approximation): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2) (smooth transition from linear to nonlinear compliance)
- Johnson–Cook-like separable form without strain-rate term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * log(1 + c4 * Abs(epsilon))) * (1 - (c5 * T + c6)**c7) (hardening with empirical thermal softening)
- Smooth elastic–plastic transition (tanh blend): sigma = (c0 * epsilon) * (1 - tanh(c1 * (epsilon + c2))) + (c3 + c4 * epsilon**c5) * tanh(c1 * (epsilon + c2)) (elastic at small strain, plastic-like beyond yield)
- Thermally shifted yield-type rational form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 * epsilon) / (1 + c3 * Abs(epsilon)) (initial offset plus saturating hardening; temperature shifts baseline)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic modulus temperature dependence → multiply epsilon by a T-dependent prefactor (e.g., (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon or c0*T**c1*epsilon).
- Thermal expansion / stress-free strain shift → use epsilon plus a T-dependent offset (epsilon + c*(T + c_ref)) before multiplying by stiffness.
- Work hardening curvature → use epsilon**c (concave/convex depending on exponent) and allow the amplitude to vary with T to represent thermal softening.
- Saturation of hardening at large strain → use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or rational saturators in epsilon to approach a limiting stress.
- Yield-like transition behavior → use smooth blending functions (e.g., tanh of (epsilon - epsilon_y(T))) to switch from elastic to plastic regime without a hard discontinuity.
- Thermal softening toward high T → include a multiplicative factor that decreases with T (e.g., 1 - (c*T + c0)**m) to reduce flow stress as temperature rises.
- Coupled thermomechanical nonlinearity → allow T to modulate higher-order strain terms (e.g., (c0 + c1*T)*epsilon**2) since temperature effects are often stronger in plastic/nonlinear regimes than in the initial elastic slope.
- Need for absolute strain measures in fitted constitutive laws → use Abs(epsilon) in nonlinear terms to enforce symmetry between tension/compression when appropriate.
